1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Architecture Document: Istio Pilot Discovery Service

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae (mirror of istio/istio)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for **Istio Pilot's Discovery Service** subsystem. The document must explain how Pilot serves xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) configuration to proxies, translates Istio's high-level configuration into Envoy-specific resources, integrates with service registries, and supports multi-cluster deployments. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server
The central component implementing Pilot's gRPC interface for Envoy's xDS APIs. Explain:
- How it implements Envoy's xDS v3 protocol (ADS, incremental/state-of-the-world modes)
- The role of `adsClients` in tracking active proxy connections
- How configuration pushes are coordinated: debouncing, rate limiting, concurrent push limits
- Cache management for xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS)
- The lifecycle: initialization, handling new connections, shutdown

### 2. ADS and the Connection Model
The Aggregated Discovery Service stream handler. Explain:
- How `Stream()` establishes a bidirectional gRPC stream with an Envoy proxy
- The `Connection` type: wrapping the stream with proxy metadata and state
- Request processing: how `processRequest()` determines what configuration to send
- Push coordination: how `pushConnection()` transmits updates to a single proxy
- The `StartPush()` broadcast mechanism for fleet-wide updates

### 3. PushContext — Configuration Snapshot and Translation
The immutable configuration snapshot used during a push. Explain:
- What `PushContext` holds: services, destination rules, virtual services, sidecars, gateways
- How `InitContext()` rebuilds the push context when Istio config changes (CRD watches)
- Config translation: how Pilot converts Istio's `VirtualService` and `DestinationRule` into Envoy's `RouteConfiguration` and `Cluster` resources
- The relationship between push triggers (config changes, service registry updates) and push context regeneration
- Metrics and error tracking during push generation

### 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support
The service discovery layer feeding the DiscoveryServer. Explain:
- How `ServiceRegistry` (Kubernetes controller) watches K8s Services, Endpoints, and Pods
- The aggregate controller pattern for multi-registry support (K8s services + `ServiceEntry` resources)
- Multi-cluster support: how Pilot aggregates services from multiple clusters
- How endpoint updates (pod scale-up, health changes) trigger EDS pushes
- The relationship between the service registry and xDS: when does a service change trigger CDS vs. EDS?

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path from Istio config change → DiscoveryServer → xDS push to Envoy proxies
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Istio (custom config translation, external service registries, telemetry plugins)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (config validation, push failures, proxy disconnects) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the istio/istio repository (e.g., `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`, `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`)

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or struct dump
- Do NOT fabricate type names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Istio components outside the Pilot discovery path (e.g., Citadel, Galley, sidecar injection)

**File:** `/workspace/documentation.md`

### Contents:

1. **DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server** (Section 1)

   - `Connection` object structure

   - Request processing logic
   - Push coordination mechanisms
   - Fleet-wide update flow via `StartPush()`

   - Structure and all indexes (services, virtual services, destination rules, sidecars, gateways, policies)
   - `InitContext()` initialization process
   - How Istio config translates to Envoy resources
   - Proxy status tracking and metrics
   - Lock-free design for performance

4. **Service Registry and Multi-Cluster** (Section 4)
   - ServiceRegistry interface
   - Kubernetes controller watching Services, Endpoints, Pods
   - Aggregate controller for multi-registry/multi-cluster support
   - EDS (Endpoint Discovery Service) integration
   - ServiceEntry CRD support

5. **Data Flow Walkthrough**
   - Complete trace from config change → PushContext init → per-proxy generation → Envoy update

   - Authorization policies
   - Event handlers

During\n191: \t\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\n192: \t\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. 19. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot's Discovery Service Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nIstio's **Pilot Discovery Service** is the core control plane component that implements Envoy's xDS (Extensible Discovery Service) protocol, translating Istio's high-level networking configuration into concrete, proxy-ready Envoy resources. This document details the architecture of this subsystem, focusing on how configuration flows from Kubernetes API servers and Istio resources through Pilot to connected Envoy proxies.\n\nAt its core, the Discovery Service answers three fundamental questions for every connected Envoy proxy:\n1. **What services exist** and where are their endpoints? (EDS/CDS)\n2. **How should traffic route** to those services? (RDS/LDS)\n3. **What security policies apply** to this traffic? (SDS/RBAC)\n\nThe Discovery Service does this by maintaining a push-based streaming connection with each proxy, broadcasting updates whenever the mesh configuration changes.\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\nThe `DiscoveryServer` is Pilot's central component implementing Envoy's xDS v3 protocol. It manages proxy connections, orchestrates configuration updates, and implements both state-of-the-world (SotW) and incremental (delta) xDS APIs.\n\n### Core Structure\n\n```go\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n  Env *model.Environment              // Mesh configuration, service registry, config store\n  Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator  // Type-specific config generators\n  adsClients map[string]*Connection   // Active proxy connections\n  pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest // Debouncing buffer\n  pushQueue *PushQueue                // Queue for rate-limited pushes\n  Cache model.XdsCache                // xDS resource cache\n}\n```\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\n1. **Initialization** (`CachesSynced()` \u2192 `serverReady`)\n   - The server waits for all Kubernetes and config watchers to synchronize before accepting proxy connections\n   - This prevents incomplete configuration delivery to early-connecting proxies\n   - See `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/server.go` line 856-862 for readiness probing\n\n2. **Starting Services** (`Start()`)\n   - Launches goroutines for handling updates, periodic metrics, push queue processing, and cache maintenance\n   - Each component runs independently with minimal locking\n\n3. **Shutdown** (`Shutdown()`)\n   - Closes JWT key resolver and gracefully drains the push queue\n   - Ensures in-flight pushes complete before termination\n\n### Push Coordination Mechanism\n\nThe Discovery Server implements a multi-stage pipeline to coordinate configuration pushes efficiently:\n\n**Stage 1: Debouncing** (`pushChannel`)\n- Configuration changes are buffered in a debounce channel (10-element buffer by default)\n- The `handleUpdates()` goroutine waits for quiescence before triggering a full push\n- Prevents cascading re-computations if multiple config changes arrive rapidly\n- Debounce timing is configurable via `DebounceOptions` (default: 100ms debounce, 10s max)\n\n**Stage 2: Push Context Initialization** (`initPushContext()`)\n- When debouncing completes, a new `PushContext` snapshot is created\n- This is the most expensive operation\u2014translating all Istio config to Envoy resources\n- Includes computing sidecar scopes, merging destination rules, and building route tables\n- Recorded in metrics: `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds`\n\n**Stage 3: Push Queue** (`pushQueue`)\n- The initialized push context is queued for broadcast\n- Concurrency is limited by `concurrentPushLimit` (default: 100 concurrent pushes)\n- Prevents resource exhaustion and ensures fair distribution of CPU time\n\n**Stage 4: Per-Proxy Push** (`pushConnection()`)\n- Each connected proxy receives tailored configuration based on its sidecar scope\n- Unused resources are filtered out (e.g., a proxy only sees services in its namespace or exported to it)\n- See `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` lines 365-446 for `computeProxyState()` logic\n\n### XDS Protocol Implementation\n\nThe Discovery Server implements both **Aggregated** (ADS) and **Delta** discovery services:\n\n- **ADS (State-of-the-World)**: `StreamAggregatedResources()` \u2192 delegates to `Stream()`\n  - Client sends a request with a list of resource names and expected version\n  - Server responds with the full set of resources for that type\n  - Ensures strong consistency but higher bandwidth\n\n- **Delta**: `StreamDeltas()`\n  - Client increments subscriptions or removes old resources\n  - Server sends only the resources that changed\n  - Lower bandwidth, requires client-side state tracking\n  - Implementation in `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`\n\n### Configuration Translation Layers\n\nThe `findGenerator()` function selects the appropriate config generator for each resource type, following a priority order:\n\n1. **Custom generator per proxy metadata + type**: `Generators[\"metadata-tag/TypeUrl\"]`\n2. **Custom generator per proxy type + TypeUrl**: `Generators[\"sidecar/cds\"]`, `Generators[\"gateway/lds\"]`\n3. **Global generator for type**: `Generators[\"cds\"]`\n4. **Fallback**: Default `MCP` generator (config store based)\n\nThis extensibility allows users to inject custom logic for specific proxy types or configurations.\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`\n\nThe ADS handler manages individual proxy connections, translating low-level xDS requests into high-level push notifications.\n\n### Connection Object\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n  xds.Connection           // Base gRPC stream wrapper\n  node *core.Node          // Original Envoy node metadata\n  proxy *model.Proxy       // Parsed proxy metadata and state\n  s *DiscoveryServer       // Parent server for config generation\n  deltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream  // For delta API\n}\n```\n\nThe `Connection` bridges the gRPC layer (generic xDS protocol) and the Pilot-specific model layer (mesh configuration, service registry).\n\n### Stream Lifecycle: `Stream()`\n\nThe entry point for all proxy connections:\n\n1. **Rate Limiting** (line 215-217)\n   - Rejects new connections if request rate exceeds configured threshold\n   - Prevents thundering herd during Pilot restarts\n\n2. **Authentication** (line 220-228)\n   - Extracts security credentials from the gRPC context\n   - Pilots can be configured with authenticators (e.g., mTLS, SPIFFE)\n   - Returns the proxy's authenticated identity\n\n3. **Push Context Initialization** (line 231)\n   - Initializes the current push context if not already done\n   - Lazy initialization: only runs once per push context\n\n4. **Connection Registration** (line 232-235)\n   - Creates a new `Connection` object wrapping the stream\n   - Delegates to the shared `xds.Stream()` loop in `pkg/xds/server.go`\n   - The loop handles request/push serialization in a single goroutine per connection\n\n### Connection Initialization: `initConnection()`\n\nOnce the stream is established, the proxy's initial state is computed:\n\n1. **Metadata Parsing** (line 240-244)\n   - Extracts workload metadata from the Envoy `Node` message\n   - Populates pod labels, service account, cluster ID, etc.\n   - See `model.ParseMetadata()` in `pilot/pkg/model/` for the metadata schema\n\n2. **Cluster Alias Resolution** (line 246-248)\n   - Multi-cluster deployments may use cluster aliases\n   - Maps cluster IDs to canonical identities for cross-cluster routing\n\n3. **Authorization** (line 262-264)\n   - Checks if the proxy's identity is authorized to connect\n   - Enforced by `model.Authorizers` (customizable per installation)\n\n4. **Connection Registration** (line 271)\n   - Adds the connection to `adsClients` map for push broadcasting\n   - Timing is critical: registered *before* full initialization completes\n   - This ensures pushes don't race past initialization (see comment on line 267-270)\n\n5. **Proxy State Initialization** (line 277-280)\n   - `computeProxyState()` computes sidecar scope, service targets, gateway configuration\n   - Expensive operations; only done once per connection\n\n### Request Processing: `processRequest()`\n\nWhen a proxy sends a discovery request:\n\n1. **Determine Response Requirement** (line 155-158)\n   - Uses `xds.ShouldRespond()` to check if the response differs from the last ack\n   - Avoids redundant responses for duplicate requests (nonce matches)\n   - Extracts delta (subscribed vs. unsubscribed resources) if applicable\n\n2. **Build Push Request** (line 160-171)\n   - Creates an internal `PushRequest` with `Full: true`\n   - Captures the proxy's `LastPushContext` to ensure monotonic versioning\n   - Uses `con.proxy.LastPushTime` to ensure cache freshness\n\n3. **Sidecar Scope Update** (line 173-179)\n   - If the proxy's sidecar scope version doesn't match the current push context version,\n     recomputes the scope before responding\n   - Handles a race condition where the push context advances before the proxy's scope is updated\n\n4. **Configuration Generation** (line 180)\n   - Delegates to `pushXds()` which calls the appropriate generator for the resource type\n   - See Section 1 for generator selection logic\n\n### Push Coordination: `pushConnection()`\n\nWhen the DiscoveryServer broadcasts to all proxies:\n\n1. **Per-Proxy Filtering** (ads.go lines 365-446, `computeProxyState()`)\n   - Service targets are recomputed only if the push includes service or config changes\n   - Sidecar scope is recomputed if there are virtual service or sidecar config updates\n   - Gateway configuration is recomputed if services have changed\n\n2. **Resource Generation** (xdsgen.go lines 101-125)\n   - Calls `gen.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, pushRequest)`\n   - Generator returns the Envoy resources (Clusters, Routes, Listeners, Endpoints, etc.)\n   - If no changes detected, returns `nil` to skip the response (optimization)\n\n3. **Response Transmission**\n   - Wraps the resources in a `DiscoveryResponse` with version info and nonce\n   - Sends over the gRPC stream\n   - Proxy should ACK with the nonce to confirm receipt\n\n### StartPush() \u2014 Fleet-Wide Updates\n\nWhen configuration changes (e.g., a VirtualService is edited):\n\n1. `ConfigUpdate()` is called with the changed resource type\n2. `handleUpdates()` debounces rapid changes\n3. `initPushContext()` creates the new snapshot\n4. `AdsPushAll()` iterates all active connections and queues a push event\n5. Each connection's event loop calls `pushConnection()` asynchronously\n6. Concurrent pushes are limited by `concurrentPushLimit` semaphore\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`, `pilot/pkg/model/context.go`\n\nThe `PushContext` is an immutable snapshot of the mesh configuration at a point in time. It serves as the single source of truth during configuration generation, enabling lock-free lookups and efficient incremental updates.\n\n### Structure and Indexes\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n  // Indexes of Istio configuration resources\n  ServiceIndex serviceIndex              // Services keyed by hostname, namespace, visibility\n  virtualServiceIndex virtualServiceIndex  // Virtual services by gateway and namespace\n  destinationRuleIndex destinationRuleIndex // Destination rules by service\n  sidecarIndex sidecarIndex               // Sidecar resources for scope computation\n  gatewayIndex gatewayIndex               // Gateway resources\n\n  // Policy indexes\n  AuthnPolicies *AuthenticationPolicies    // RequestAuthentication policies\n  AuthzPolicies *AuthorizationPolicies     // Authorization policies (RBAC)\n  Telemetry *Telemetries                   // Telemetry resources\n  ProxyConfigs *ProxyConfigs               // ProxyConfig customizations\n\n  // Metadata\n  Mesh *meshconfig.MeshConfig              // Global mesh settings\n  Networks *meshconfig.MeshNetworks        // Multi-cluster network topology\n  PushVersion string                       // Unique version identifier\n  InitDone atomic.Bool                     // Marks successful initialization\n  ProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus  // Push metrics per proxy\n}\n```\n\n### Initialization: `InitContext()`\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` line 1345\n\nThe initialization process rebuilds the push context from the current state of:\n- The Kubernetes API (services, endpoints, pods)\n- The config store (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, etc.)\n- The service registry (aggregated from multiple clusters)\n\n**Key phases:**\n\n1. **Check Early Exit** (line 1350-1351)\n   - If `InitDone` is already true, exit early (initialization is idempotent)\n   - Prevents concurrent initialization of the same context\n\n2. **Service Index Rebuild** (`rebuildServiceIndex()`)\n   - Queries all services from the environment's service registry\n   - Partitions services by visibility (private to namespace, exported, or public)\n   - Builds hostname\u2192namespace\u2192service maps for O(1) lookup\n   - Caches instance lists by port (for EDS generation)\n\n3. **Config-Based Indexes** (`rebuildVirtualServiceIndex()`, etc.)\n   - Reads VirtualServices from the config store, groups by gateway and namespace\n   - Reads DestinationRules, merges by service host\n   - Reads Sidecars, computes derived defaults for namespaces lacking explicit sidecars\n   - Reads Gateways, organizes by namespace\n\n4. **Policy Indexes**\n   - Builds authorization policy index from cluster policies\n   - Builds authentication policy index (if enabled)\n   - Organizes by namespace and scope (mesh-wide vs. namespace-local)\n\n5. **Marking Completion** (line `InitDone.Store(true)`)\n   - Signals that the context is ready for use\n   - Downstream generators can proceed with configuration generation\n\n**Performance Considerations:**\n- Initialization is expensive (typically 100ms\u20131s for large clusters)\n- Recorded in metrics: `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds` (buckets: 0.01s, 0.1s, 0.5s, 1s, 3s, 5s)\n- Happens once per config change, not per proxy\u2014shared across all proxies receiving the same push\n\n### Configuration Translation\n\nGenerators use the PushContext to translate Istio config to Envoy:\n\n**Example: Virtual Service \u2192 Route Configuration**\n1. Generator receives request for `RDS` (Route Discovery Service)\n2. Queries `ps.virtualServiceIndex` for VirtualServices matching the destination\n3. For each VirtualService:\n   - Extracts HTTP routes, TCP routes, etc.\n   - Merges with timeout, retry, and circuit breaker settings from DestinationRule\n   - Converts to Envoy `RouteConfiguration` proto\n4. Returns list of Envoy routes, indexed by domain\n\n**Example: Service \u2192 Cluster Configuration**\n1. Generator receives request for `CDS` (Cluster Discovery Service)\n2. Iterates services in the proxy's sidecar scope\n3. For each service:\n   - Creates an Envoy `Cluster` with load balancing policy from DestinationRule\n   - Configures TLS settings (mTLS, CA certs, SNI)\n   - Sets up outlier detection and circuit breaker thresholds\n4. Returns list of Envoy clusters\n\n### Proxy Status Tracking\n\nPushContext tracks push outcomes per proxy:\n\n```go\nProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus\n// Keyed by: error code \u2192 proxy ID \u2192 status details\n```\n\n**Recorded Information:**\n- Proxy configuration errors (e.g., \"no service found for destination\")\n- Endpoint errors (e.g., \"pod not ready\")\n- Conflict warnings (e.g., \"duplicate cluster definitions\")\n- Push timing metrics\n\n**Visibility:** Exposed via debug endpoints (`/debug/push_status`, `/debug/pushcontext`) and Prometheus metrics.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`, `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\nThe service registry is the discovery layer feeding dynamic endpoint and service information to the DiscoveryServer. It bridges Kubernetes API watchers with Istio's networking abstractions.\n\n### ServiceRegistry Interface\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n  // Services returns all services in the mesh\n  Services() []*Service\n\n  // GetService returns the service by hostname\n  GetService(hostname host.Name) *Service\n\n  // InstancesByPort returns instances (pods) of a service on a specific port\n  InstancesByPort(svc *Service, port int, labels labels.Collection) []*IstioEndpoint\n\n  // ManagementPorts returns the management ports of a pod\n  ManagementPorts(pod *model.Pod) model.PortList\n}\n\ntype Controller interface {\n  // AppendServiceHandler registers a callback for service changes\n  AppendServiceHandler(handler model.EventHandler)\n\n  // AppendInstanceHandler registers a callback for endpoint changes\n  AppendInstanceHandler(handler model.EventHandler)\n\n  // Run starts the controller's watch loops\n  Run(stop <-chan struct{})\n}\n```\n\n### Kubernetes Controller\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/`\n\nThe Kubernetes controller watches K8s resources and translates them to Istio model:\n\n**Watched Resources:**\n1. **Services** \u2192 `model.Service`\n   - Port mappings, selectors, service type (ClusterIP, LoadBalancer, ExternalName)\n   - Cached in service registry, indexed by hostname\n\n2. **Endpoints** \u2192 `model.IstioEndpoint`\n   - Pod IPs, ports, health status, zone information\n   - Translated to Envoy endpoint assignments (EDS)\n   - Watched per-service for efficient updates\n\n3. **Pods** \u2192 Workload metadata\n   - Labels, annotations, node affinity\n   - Used to populate sidecar proxy labels\n   - Enables locality-aware routing (region/zone awareness)\n\n**Event Propagation:**\n- Service change \u2192 triggers `EventHandler.Handle()` with event type and changed service\n- Endpoint change \u2192 triggers EDS-specific handler\n- Handler calls back to DiscoveryServer (`SvcUpdate()`, `EDSUpdate()`)\n\n### Aggregate Controller\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`\n\nMulti-cluster Istio deployments use the aggregate controller to combine service registries:\n\n```go\ntype Controller struct {\n  registries []serviceregistry.Instance\n  // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Features:**\n1. **Multi-Registry Support**\n   - Aggregates services from Kubernetes (local cluster)\n   - Aggregates services from remote clusters (via API-server-based federation)\n   - Aggregates services from ServiceEntry CRDs (external services)\n\n2. **Service Deduplication**\n   - If the same service exists in multiple registries (e.g., local K8s + ServiceEntry),\n     the aggregate controller merges them\n   - Prevents duplicate endpoint lists\n\n3. **Cross-Cluster Networking**\n   - Maintains network topology information (which cluster, which network)\n   - Enables Envoy to select endpoints based on proximity\n\n**Multi-Cluster Example:**\n- Cluster A has `my-service` with 3 pods in us-west-2\n- Cluster B (federated) has `my-service` with 2 pods in eu-west-1\n- Aggregate controller returns all 5 endpoints\n- Envoy can route locally or cross-cluster based on locality preferences\n\n### EDS (Endpoint Discovery Service) Integration\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\nEDS pushes endpoint information to Envoy as pods scale up/down or health status changes.\n\n**Handlers:**\n- `EDSUpdate()` \u2014 Called when endpoints change, triggers incremental push\n- `EDSCacheUpdate()` \u2014 Updates cache without requesting a push (optimization for frequent changes)\n\n**Optimization:**\n- EDS updates are more frequent than full config pushes (pods restart, health changes)\n- Can be debounced separately via `enableEDSDebounce` feature flag\n- Avoids recomputing routes/clusters if only endpoints changed\n\n### ServiceEntry Support\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/`\n\nServiceEntry CRDs allow declaring external services (not in Kubernetes):\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: ServiceEntry\nmetadata:\n  name: external-api\nspec:\n  hosts:\n  - api.example.com\n  ports:\n  - number: 443\n    name: https\n    protocol: HTTPS\n  endpoints:\n  - address: api.example.com\n    ports:\n      https: 443\n```\n\nThe service entry controller:\n1. Watches ServiceEntry resources\n2. Converts them to `model.Service` and `model.IstioEndpoint`\n3. Registers with the aggregate controller\n4. Merges with Kubernetes-discovered services\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: From Config Change to Envoy Update\n\nThis section traces the complete path of a configuration change through the Discovery Service.\n\n### Scenario: User Updates a VirtualService\n\n**Step 1: Config Change Detection**\n```\nKubernetes API Server\n  \u2514\u2500> Istio ConfigController watches VirtualService CRD\n      \u2514\u2500> Calls DiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate(PushRequest)\n          - ConfigsUpdated: {kind/group/name of changed VirtualService}\n          - Full: false (incremental update)\n```\n\n**Step 2: Debouncing**\n```\nDiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate()\n  \u2514\u2500> Sends PushRequest to pushChannel (10-element buffer)\n      \u2514\u2500> handleUpdates() goroutine waits for quiescence (default: 100ms)\n          \u2514\u2500> If no new changes arrive, proceeds to InitContext\n```\n\n**Step 3: Push Context Initialization**\n```\ninitPushContext()\n  \u2514\u2500> Creates new PushContext snapshot\n      \u2514\u2500> Calls ps.InitContext(env, oldPushContext, pushRequest)\n          \u2514\u2500> rebuildVirtualServiceIndex()\n              - Reads *all* VirtualServices from config store\n              - Re-indexes by gateway, namespace, destination\n          \u2514\u2500> Existing indexes (services, endpoints) reused from oldPushContext\n                (optimization: only recompute affected resources)\n          \u2514\u2500> Sets PushVersion = NextVersion() (timestamp-based)\n      \u2514\u2500> Stores in Environment.SetPushContext(push)\n      \u2514\u2500> Drops cache entries for affected resource types\n```\n\n**Step 4: Broadcast to All Proxies**\n```\nAdsPushAll(pushRequest)\n  \u2514\u2500> Iterates DiscoveryServer.adsClients\n      \u2514\u2500> For each Connection:\n          \u2514\u2500> Queues pushConnection() to pushQueue\n              \u2514\u2500> concurrentPushLimit semaphore regulates parallelism\n                  \u2514\u2500> computeProxyState(proxy, pushRequest)\n                      - Recomputes proxy's sidecar scope (if VirtualService affects it)\n                      - Scope determines which services/routes are relevant\n                  \u2514\u2500> Calls pushXds() for each watched resource type\n                      \u2514\u2500> findGenerator(typeURL, connection)\n                          - Selects appropriate generator (LdsGenerator, RdsGenerator, etc.)\n                      \u2514\u2500> gen.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, pushRequest)\n                          - Translates Istio config to Envoy proto\n                          - Uses PushContext snapshot from pushRequest\n                      \u2514\u2500> If gen.Generate() returns a DiscoveryResponse:\n                          \u2514\u2500> Sends over gRPC stream to proxy\n                              \u2514\u2500> Proxy ACKs with version/nonce\n```\n\n**Step 5: Proxy Receives Update**\n```\nEnvoy Proxy (receiving DiscoveryResponse for RDS)\n  \u2514\u2500> Parses RouteConfiguration from response\n      \u2514\u2500> Validates routes (checks all upstream clusters exist)\n      \u2514\u2500> Sends ACK with nonce from DiscoveryResponse\n          \u2514\u2500> DiscoveryServer records: proxy config updated successfully\n      \u2514\u2500> Hot-reloads routes without dropping active connections\n```\n\n**Performance Metrics:**\n- `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds`: How long to rebuild push context\n- `pilot_debounce_time`: Total delay from config change to push queue\n- `pilot_xds_push_time`: Per-proxy push generation time\n- `pilot_xds_calls_total`: Number of xDS Generate() calls\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nThe Discovery Service is designed with several extension points for custom behavior:\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\nUsers can inject custom `XdsResourceGenerator` implementations:\n\n```go\ntype CustomGenerator struct{}\n\nfunc (g *CustomGenerator) Generate(proxy *model.Proxy, w *model.WatchedResource, req *model.PushRequest) ([]*discovery.Resource, model.XdsLogDetails, error) {\n  // Custom logic to generate Envoy resources\n  // E.g., fetch data from external API, apply custom transformations\n  return resources, logDetails, nil\n}\n\n// Register in bootstrap\ngenerators[\"custom-type/lds\"] = &CustomGenerator{}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom load balancing logic (e.g., weighted round-robin based on external metrics)\n- Dynamic cluster configuration (e.g., auto-discovery of database hosts)\n- Security policy injection (e.g., enforce custom TLS settings)\n\n**Location:** Registered in `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/discovery.go`\n\n### 2. Service Registry Plugins\n\nCustom service discovery backends can be plugged in:\n\n```go\ntype CustomRegistry struct{}\n\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) Services() []*model.Service {\n  // Query external service registry (Consul, Eureka, etc.)\n}\n\n// Register as additional registry\naggregate.AddRegistry(customRegistry)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Integrate legacy service discovery (Consul, Eureka)\n- Cloud-provider-specific service discovery\n- Custom endpoint selection logic\n\n### 3. Authorization Policies\n\nDiscoveryServer supports pluggable authorization:\n\n```go\ntype CustomAuthorizer struct{}\n\nfunc (a *CustomAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attributes ...string) error {\n  // Custom authorization logic (e.g., check external RBAC system)\n  return nil // or error if unauthorized\n}\n\n// Configure in Pilot\nenv.Authorizers = append(env.Authorizers, &CustomAuthorizer{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- External RBAC systems (LDAP, OIDC)\n- Custom certificate validation\n- Traffic policy enforcement\n\n### 4. Event Handlers\n\nServices and configs support custom event handlers:\n\n```go\nhandler := func(event model.Event) {\n  // React to configuration changes\n  // E.g., update external systems, trigger deployments\n}\n\ncontroller.AppendServiceHandler(handler)\nconfigController.RegisterEventHandler(handler)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Trigger canary deployments on config changes\n- Sync Pilot config to other systems\n- Custom audit logging\n\n### 5. Config Transformations via EnvoyFilter\n\nUsers can inject custom Envoy configuration without modifying Pilot:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: EnvoyFilter\nmetadata:\n  name: custom-filter\nspec:\n  workloadSelector:\n    labels:\n      app: myapp\n  configPatches:\n  - applyTo: HTTP_FILTER\n    match:\n      context: SIDECAR_INBOUND\n    patch:\n      operation: INSERT_BEFORE\n      value:\n        name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager\n        # ... custom filter config\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Configuration Validation Errors\n\nIf a VirtualService or DestinationRule has invalid syntax:\n\n1. ConfigController's validator rejects it before storing\n2. If already stored but later invalid:\n   - Generators detect missing referenced resources\n   - Log warnings/errors in proxy status\n   - Continue serving (fail-safe, don't drop proxies)\n\n**Visible in:**\n- Proxy push status: `ProxyStatus[error_code][proxy_id]`\n- Debug endpoints: `/debug/push_status`, `/debug/pushcontext`\n- Prometheus metrics: `pilot_proxy_status_*`\n\n### Push Failures\n\nIf a proxy disconnect during push:\n\n1. Connection closes (gRPC stream ends)\n2. `closeConnection()` removes from `adsClients`\n3. Remaining proxies continue receiving updates\n4. Proxy reconnects later, gets latest config\n\n### Service Registry Errors\n\nIf Kubernetes API is unavailable:\n\n1. Controller's sync loop stalls (but doesn't crash)\n2. `CachesSynced()` blocks, preventing Pilot readiness\n3. Once API recovers, resync occurs automatically\n4. Proxies remain connected, use cached configuration\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Push Scaling\n\nFor a mesh with N proxies:\n\n1. **Push Context Init**: O(1) per config change (not per proxy)\n2. **Per-Proxy Generation**: O(N) proxies \u00d7 O(M) config \u2192 O(N\u00d7M) total\n3. **Concurrency**: Limited by `concurrentPushLimit` (default: 100)\n   - Prevents overwhelming Pilot's CPU and memory\n   - Trade-off: slower update propagation in very large clusters\n\n### Debouncing\n\nRapid config changes are coalesced:\n\n- 10 VirtualService changes in 50ms \u2192 1 push context init (not 10)\n- Trade-off: 100ms delay vs. recomputation cost\n- Configurable via `DebounceAfter`, `DebounceMax`\n\n### Caching\n\nXDS resources are cached to avoid re-generation:\n\n- Keyed by proxy ID + resource type + config hash\n- Cleared on config change (invalidation is simple hash-based)\n- Significantly speeds up subsequent requests for same resource\n\n---\n\n## Source Files Reference\n\n| Component | File |\n|-----------|------|\n| DiscoveryServer (core) | `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` |\n| ADS stream handling | `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` |\n| Delta XDS | `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go` |\n| PushContext | `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` |\n| Config translation | `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` |\n| CDS (Cluster Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go` |\n| EDS (Endpoint Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` |\n| LDS (Listener Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go` |\n| RDS (Route Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go` |\n| SDS (Secret Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/sds.go` |\n| Kubernetes service registry | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go` |\n| Aggregate registry | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go` |\n| ServiceEntry registry | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/controller.go` |\n| Bootstrap & initialization | `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/discovery.go`, `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/server.go` |\n| Testing utilities | `pilot/test/xds/fake.go` |\n| Metrics | `pilot/pkg/xds/monitoring.go` |\n| Debug handlers | `pilot/pkg/xds/debug.go` |\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Istio Pilot Discovery Service is a sophisticated distributed system that translates high-level mesh configuration into concrete Envoy proxy updates. Its architecture emphasizes:\n\n1. **Scalability**: Deferred initialization, debouncing, caching, and concurrency controls\n2. **Correctness**: Monotonically increasing versions, lock-free reads via snapshots\n3. **Extensibility**: Pluggable generators, registries, authorizers, and event handlers\n4. **Observability**: Comprehensive metrics, debug endpoints, and error tracking\n\nUnderstanding these layers is crucial for:\n- Debugging mesh configuration issues\n- Tuning Pilot performance for large clusters\n- Extending Istio with custom logic\n- Troubleshooting proxy synchronization problems\n",

{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot's Discovery Service Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nIstio's **Pilot Discovery Service** is the core control plane component that implements Envoy's xDS (Extensible Discovery Service) protocol, translating Istio's high-level networking configuration into concrete, proxy-ready Envoy resources. This document details the architecture of this subsystem, focusing on how configuration flows from Kubernetes API servers and Istio resources through Pilot to connected Envoy proxies.\n\nAt its core, the Discovery Service answers three fundamental questions for every connected Envoy proxy:\n1. **What services exist** and where are their endpoints? (EDS/CDS)\n2. **How should traffic route** to those services? (RDS/LDS)\n3. **What security policies apply** to this traffic? (SDS/RBAC)\n\nThe Discovery Service does this by maintaining a push-based streaming connection with each proxy, broadcasting updates whenever the mesh configuration changes.\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\nThe `DiscoveryServer` is Pilot's central component implementing Envoy's xDS v3 protocol. It manages proxy connections, orchestrates configuration updates, and implements both state-of-the-world (SotW) and incremental (delta) xDS APIs.\n\n### Core Structure\n\n```go\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n  Env *model.Environment              // Mesh configuration, service registry, config store\n  Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator  // Type-specific config generators\n  adsClients map[string]*Connection   // Active proxy connections\n  pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest // Debouncing buffer\n  pushQueue *PushQueue                // Queue for rate-limited pushes\n  Cache model.XdsCache                // xDS resource cache\n}\n```\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\n1. **Initialization** (`CachesSynced()` \u2192 `serverReady`)\n   - The server waits for all Kubernetes and config watchers to synchronize before accepting proxy connections\n   - This prevents incomplete configuration delivery to early-connecting proxies\n   - See `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/server.go` line 856-862 for readiness probing\n\n2. **Starting Services** (`Start()`)\n   - Launches goroutines for handling updates, periodic metrics, push queue processing, and cache maintenance\n   - Each component runs independently with minimal locking\n\n3. **Shutdown** (`Shutdown()`)\n   - Closes JWT key resolver and gracefully drains the push queue\n   - Ensures in-flight pushes complete before termination\n\n### Push Coordination Mechanism\n\nThe Discovery Server implements a multi-stage pipeline to coordinate configuration pushes efficiently:\n\n**Stage 1: Debouncing** (`pushChannel`)\n- Configuration changes are buffered in a debounce channel (10-element buffer by default)\n- The `handleUpdates()` goroutine waits for quiescence before triggering a full push\n- Prevents cascading re-computations if multiple config changes arrive rapidly\n- Debounce timing is configurable via `DebounceOptions` (default: 100ms debounce, 10s max)\n\n**Stage 2: Push Context Initialization** (`initPushContext()`)\n- When debouncing completes, a new `PushContext` snapshot is created\n- This is the most expensive operation\u2014translating all Istio config to Envoy resources\n- Includes computing sidecar scopes, merging destination rules, and building route tables\n- Recorded in metrics: `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds`\n\n**Stage 3: Push Queue** (`pushQueue`)\n- The initialized push context is queued for broadcast\n- Concurrency is limited by `concurrentPushLimit` (default: 100 concurrent pushes)\n- Prevents resource exhaustion and ensures fair distribution of CPU time\n\n**Stage 4: Per-Proxy Push** (`pushConnection()`)\n- Each connected proxy receives tailored configuration based on its sidecar scope\n- Unused resources are filtered out (e.g., a proxy only sees services in its namespace or exported to it)\n- See `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` lines 365-446 for `computeProxyState()` logic\n\n### XDS Protocol Implementation\n\nThe Discovery Server implements both **Aggregated** (ADS) and **Delta** discovery services:\n\n- **ADS (State-of-the-World)**: `StreamAggregatedResources()` \u2192 delegates to `Stream()`\n  - Client sends a request with a list of resource names and expected version\n  - Server responds with the full set of resources for that type\n  - Ensures strong consistency but higher bandwidth\n\n- **Delta**: `StreamDeltas()`\n  - Client increments subscriptions or removes old resources\n  - Server sends only the resources that changed\n  - Lower bandwidth, requires client-side state tracking\n  - Implementation in `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`\n\n### Configuration Translation Layers\n\nThe `findGenerator()` function selects the appropriate config generator for each resource type, following a priority order:\n\n1. **Custom generator per proxy metadata + type**: `Generators[\"metadata-tag/TypeUrl\"]`\n2. **Custom generator per proxy type + TypeUrl**: `Generators[\"sidecar/cds\"]`, `Generators[\"gateway/lds\"]`\n3. **Global generator for type**: `Generators[\"cds\"]`\n4. **Fallback**: Default `MCP` generator (config store based)\n\nThis extensibility allows users to inject custom logic for specific proxy types or configurations.\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`\n\nThe ADS handler manages individual proxy connections, translating low-level xDS requests into high-level push notifications.\n\n### Connection Object\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n  xds.Connection           // Base gRPC stream wrapper\n  node *core.Node          // Original Envoy node metadata\n  proxy *model.Proxy       // Parsed proxy metadata and state\n  s *DiscoveryServer       // Parent server for config generation\n  deltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream  // For delta API\n}\n```\n\nThe `Connection` bridges the gRPC layer (generic xDS protocol) and the Pilot-specific model layer (mesh configuration, service registry).\n\n### Stream Lifecycle: `Stream()`\n\nThe entry point for all proxy connections:\n\n1. **Rate Limiting** (line 215-217)\n   - Rejects new connections if request rate exceeds configured threshold\n   - Prevents thundering herd during Pilot restarts\n\n2. **Authentication** (line 220-228)\n   - Extracts security credentials from the gRPC context\n   - Pilots can be configured with authenticators (e.g., mTLS, SPIFFE)\n   - Returns the proxy's authenticated identity\n\n3. **Push Context Initialization** (line 231)\n   - Initializes the current push context if not already done\n   - Lazy initialization: only runs once per push context\n\n4. **Connection Registration** (line 232-235)\n   - Creates a new `Connection` object wrapping the stream\n   - Delegates to the shared `xds.Stream()` loop in `pkg/xds/server.go`\n   - The loop handles request/push serialization in a single goroutine per connection\n\n### Connection Initialization: `initConnection()`\n\nOnce the stream is established, the proxy's initial state is computed:\n\n1. **Metadata Parsing** (line 240-244)\n   - Extracts workload metadata from the Envoy `Node` message\n   - Populates pod labels, service account, cluster ID, etc.\n   - See `model.ParseMetadata()` in `pilot/pkg/model/` for the metadata schema\n\n2. **Cluster Alias Resolution** (line 246-248)\n   - Multi-cluster deployments may use cluster aliases\n   - Maps cluster IDs to canonical identities for cross-cluster routing\n\n3. **Authorization** (line 262-264)\n   - Checks if the proxy's identity is authorized to connect\n   - Enforced by `model.Authorizers` (customizable per installation)\n\n4. **Connection Registration** (line 271)\n   - Adds the connection to `adsClients` map for push broadcasting\n   - Timing is critical: registered *before* full initialization completes\n   - This ensures pushes don't race past initialization (see comment on line 267-270)\n\n5. **Proxy State Initialization** (line 277-280)\n   - `computeProxyState()` computes sidecar scope, service targets, gateway configuration\n   - Expensive operations; only done once per connection\n\n### Request Processing: `processRequest()`\n\nWhen a proxy sends a discovery request:\n\n1. **Determine Response Requirement** (line 155-158)\n   - Uses `xds.ShouldRespond()` to check if the response differs from the last ack\n   - Avoids redundant responses for duplicate requests (nonce matches)\n   - Extracts delta (subscribed vs. unsubscribed resources) if applicable\n\n2. **Build Push Request** (line 160-171)\n   - Creates an internal `PushRequest` with `Full: true`\n   - Captures the proxy's `LastPushContext` to ensure monotonic versioning\n   - Uses `con.proxy.LastPushTime` to ensure cache freshness\n\n3. **Sidecar Scope Update** (line 173-179)\n   - If the proxy's sidecar scope version doesn't match the current push context version,\n     recomputes the scope before responding\n   - Handles a race condition where the push context advances before the proxy's scope is updated\n\n4. **Configuration Generation** (line 180)\n   - Delegates to `pushXds()` which calls the appropriate generator for the resource type\n   - See Section 1 for generator selection logic\n\n### Push Coordination: `pushConnection()`\n\nWhen the DiscoveryServer broadcasts to all proxies:\n\n1. **Per-Proxy Filtering** (ads.go lines 365-446, `computeProxyState()`)\n   - Service targets are recomputed only if the push includes service or config changes\n   - Sidecar scope is recomputed if there are virtual service or sidecar config updates\n   - Gateway configuration is recomputed if services have changed\n\n2. **Resource Generation** (xdsgen.go lines 101-125)\n   - Calls `gen.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, pushRequest)`\n   - Generator returns the Envoy resources (Clusters, Routes, Listeners, Endpoints, etc.)\n   - If no changes detected, returns `nil` to skip the response (optimization)\n\n3. **Response Transmission**\n   - Wraps the resources in a `DiscoveryResponse` with version info and nonce\n   - Sends over the gRPC stream\n   - Proxy should ACK with the nonce to confirm receipt\n\n### StartPush() \u2014 Fleet-Wide Updates\n\nWhen configuration changes (e.g., a VirtualService is edited):\n\n1. `ConfigUpdate()` is called with the changed resource type\n2. `handleUpdates()` debounces rapid changes\n3. `initPushContext()` creates the new snapshot\n4. `AdsPushAll()` iterates all active connections and queues a push event\n5. Each connection's event loop calls `pushConnection()` asynchronously\n6. Concurrent pushes are limited by `concurrentPushLimit` semaphore\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`, `pilot/pkg/model/context.go`\n\nThe `PushContext` is an immutable snapshot of the mesh configuration at a point in time. It serves as the single source of truth during configuration generation, enabling lock-free lookups and efficient incremental updates.\n\n### Structure and Indexes\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n  // Indexes of Istio configuration resources\n  ServiceIndex serviceIndex              // Services keyed by hostname, namespace, visibility\n  virtualServiceIndex virtualServiceIndex  // Virtual services by gateway and namespace\n  destinationRuleIndex destinationRuleIndex // Destination rules by service\n  sidecarIndex sidecarIndex               // Sidecar resources for scope computation\n  gatewayIndex gatewayIndex               // Gateway resources\n\n  // Policy indexes\n  AuthnPolicies *AuthenticationPolicies    // RequestAuthentication policies\n  AuthzPolicies *AuthorizationPolicies     // Authorization policies (RBAC)\n  Telemetry *Telemetries                   // Telemetry resources\n  ProxyConfigs *ProxyConfigs               // ProxyConfig customizations\n\n  // Metadata\n  Mesh *meshconfig.MeshConfig              // Global mesh settings\n  Networks *meshconfig.MeshNetworks        // Multi-cluster network topology\n  PushVersion string                       // Unique version identifier\n  InitDone atomic.Bool                     // Marks successful initialization\n  ProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus  // Push metrics per proxy\n}\n```\n\n### Initialization: `InitContext()`\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` line 1345\n\nThe initialization process rebuilds the push context from the current state of:\n- The Kubernetes API (services, endpoints, pods)\n- The config store (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, etc.)\n- The service registry (aggregated from multiple clusters)\n\n**Key phases:**\n\n1. **Check Early Exit** (line 1350-1351)\n   - If `InitDone` is already true, exit early (initialization is idempotent)\n   - Prevents concurrent initialization of the same context\n\n2. **Service Index Rebuild** (`rebuildServiceIndex()`)\n   - Queries all services from the environment's service registry\n   - Partitions services by visibility (private to namespace, exported, or public)\n   - Builds hostname\u2192namespace\u2192service maps for O(1) lookup\n   - Caches instance lists by port (for EDS generation)\n\n3. **Config-Based Indexes** (`rebuildVirtualServiceIndex()`, etc.)\n   - Reads VirtualServices from the config store, groups by gateway and namespace\n   - Reads DestinationRules, merges by service host\n   - Reads Sidecars, computes derived defaults for namespaces lacking explicit sidecars\n   - Reads Gateways, organizes by namespace\n\n4. **Policy Indexes**\n   - Builds authorization policy index from cluster policies\n   - Builds authentication policy index (if enabled)\n   - Organizes by namespace and scope (mesh-wide vs. namespace-local)\n\n5. **Marking Completion** (line `InitDone.Store(true)`)\n   - Signals that the context is ready for use\n   - Downstream generators can proceed with configuration generation\n\n**Performance Considerations:**\n- Initialization is expensive (typically 100ms\u20131s for large clusters)\n- Recorded in metrics: `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds` (buckets: 0.01s, 0.1s, 0.5s, 1s, 3s, 5s)\n- Happens once per config change, not per proxy\u2014shared across all proxies receiving the same push\n\n### Configuration Translation\n\nGenerators use the PushContext to translate Istio config to Envoy:\n\n**Example: Virtual Service \u2192 Route Configuration**\n1. Generator receives request for `RDS` (Route Discovery Service)\n2. Queries `ps.virtualServiceIndex` for VirtualServices matching the destination\n3. For each VirtualService:\n   - Extracts HTTP routes, TCP routes, etc.\n   - Merges with timeout, retry, and circuit breaker settings from DestinationRule\n   - Converts to Envoy `RouteConfiguration` proto\n4. Returns list of Envoy routes, indexed by domain\n\n**Example: Service \u2192 Cluster Configuration**\n1. Generator receives request for `CDS` (Cluster Discovery Service)\n2. Iterates services in the proxy's sidecar scope\n3. For each service:\n   - Creates an Envoy `Cluster` with load balancing policy from DestinationRule\n   - Configures TLS settings (mTLS, CA certs, SNI)\n   - Sets up outlier detection and circuit breaker thresholds\n4. Returns list of Envoy clusters\n\n### Proxy Status Tracking\n\nPushContext tracks push outcomes per proxy:\n\n```go\nProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus\n// Keyed by: error code \u2192 proxy ID \u2192 status details\n```\n\n**Recorded Information:**\n- Proxy configuration errors (e.g., \"no service found for destination\")\n- Endpoint errors (e.g., \"pod not ready\")\n- Conflict warnings (e.g., \"duplicate cluster definitions\")\n- Push timing metrics\n\n**Visibility:** Exposed via debug endpoints (`/debug/push_status`, `/debug/pushcontext`) and Prometheus metrics.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`, `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\nThe service registry is the discovery layer feeding dynamic endpoint and service information to the DiscoveryServer. It bridges Kubernetes API watchers with Istio's networking abstractions.\n\n### ServiceRegistry Interface\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n  // Services returns all services in the mesh\n  Services() []*Service\n\n  // GetService returns the service by hostname\n  GetService(hostname host.Name) *Service\n\n  // InstancesByPort returns instances (pods) of a service on a specific port\n  InstancesByPort(svc *Service, port int, labels labels.Collection) []*IstioEndpoint\n\n  // ManagementPorts returns the management ports of a pod\n  ManagementPorts(pod *model.Pod) model.PortList\n}\n\ntype Controller interface {\n  // AppendServiceHandler registers a callback for service changes\n  AppendServiceHandler(handler model.EventHandler)\n\n  // AppendInstanceHandler registers a callback for endpoint changes\n  AppendInstanceHandler(handler model.EventHandler)\n\n  // Run starts the controller's watch loops\n  Run(stop <-chan struct{})\n}\n```\n\n### Kubernetes Controller\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/`\n\nThe Kubernetes controller watches K8s resources and translates them to Istio model:\n\n**Watched Resources:**\n1. **Services** \u2192 `model.Service`\n   - Port mappings, selectors, service type (ClusterIP, LoadBalancer, ExternalName)\n   - Cached in service registry, indexed by hostname\n\n2. **Endpoints** \u2192 `model.IstioEndpoint`\n   - Pod IPs, ports, health status, zone information\n   - Translated to Envoy endpoint assignments (EDS)\n   - Watched per-service for efficient updates\n\n3. **Pods** \u2192 Workload metadata\n   - Labels, annotations, node affinity\n   - Used to populate sidecar proxy labels\n   - Enables locality-aware routing (region/zone awareness)\n\n**Event Propagation:**\n- Service change \u2192 triggers `EventHandler.Handle()` with event type and changed service\n- Endpoint change \u2192 triggers EDS-specific handler\n- Handler calls back to DiscoveryServer (`SvcUpdate()`, `EDSUpdate()`)\n\n### Aggregate Controller\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`\n\nMulti-cluster Istio deployments use the aggregate controller to combine service registries:\n\n```go\ntype Controller struct {\n  registries []serviceregistry.Instance\n  // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Features:**\n1. **Multi-Registry Support**\n   - Aggregates services from Kubernetes (local cluster)\n   - Aggregates services from remote clusters (via API-server-based federation)\n   - Aggregates services from ServiceEntry CRDs (external services)\n\n2. **Service Deduplication**\n   - If the same service exists in multiple registries (e.g., local K8s + ServiceEntry),\n     the aggregate controller merges them\n   - Prevents duplicate endpoint lists\n\n3. **Cross-Cluster Networking**\n   - Maintains network topology information (which cluster, which network)\n   - Enables Envoy to select endpoints based on proximity\n\n**Multi-Cluster Example:**\n- Cluster A has `my-service` with 3 pods in us-west-2\n- Cluster B (federated) has `my-service` with 2 pods in eu-west-1\n- Aggregate controller returns all 5 endpoints\n- Envoy can route locally or cross-cluster based on locality preferences\n\n### EDS (Endpoint Discovery Service) Integration\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\nEDS pushes endpoint information to Envoy as pods scale up/down or health status changes.\n\n**Handlers:**\n- `EDSUpdate()` \u2014 Called when endpoints change, triggers incremental push\n- `EDSCacheUpdate()` \u2014 Updates cache without requesting a push (optimization for frequent changes)\n\n**Optimization:**\n- EDS updates are more frequent than full config pushes (pods restart, health changes)\n- Can be debounced separately via `enableEDSDebounce` feature flag\n- Avoids recomputing routes/clusters if only endpoints changed\n\n### ServiceEntry Support\n\n**Location:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/`\n\nServiceEntry CRDs allow declaring external services (not in Kubernetes):\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: ServiceEntry\nmetadata:\n  name: external-api\nspec:\n  hosts:\n  - api.example.com\n  ports:\n  - number: 443\n    name: https\n    protocol: HTTPS\n  endpoints:\n  - address: api.example.com\n    ports:\n      https: 443\n```\n\nThe service entry controller:\n1. Watches ServiceEntry resources\n2. Converts them to `model.Service` and `model.IstioEndpoint`\n3. Registers with the aggregate controller\n4. Merges with Kubernetes-discovered services\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: From Config Change to Envoy Update\n\nThis section traces the complete path of a configuration change through the Discovery Service.\n\n### Scenario: User Updates a VirtualService\n\n**Step 1: Config Change Detection**\n```\nKubernetes API Server\n  \u2514\u2500> Istio ConfigController watches VirtualService CRD\n      \u2514\u2500> Calls DiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate(PushRequest)\n          - ConfigsUpdated: {kind/group/name of changed VirtualService}\n          - Full: false (incremental update)\n```\n\n**Step 2: Debouncing**\n```\nDiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate()\n  \u2514\u2500> Sends PushRequest to pushChannel (10-element buffer)\n      \u2514\u2500> handleUpdates() goroutine waits for quiescence (default: 100ms)\n          \u2514\u2500> If no new changes arrive, proceeds to InitContext\n```\n\n**Step 3: Push Context Initialization**\n```\ninitPushContext()\n  \u2514\u2500> Creates new PushContext snapshot\n      \u2514\u2500> Calls ps.InitContext(env, oldPushContext, pushRequest)\n          \u2514\u2500> rebuildVirtualServiceIndex()\n              - Reads *all* VirtualServices from config store\n              - Re-indexes by gateway, namespace, destination\n          \u2514\u2500> Existing indexes (services, endpoints) reused from oldPushContext\n                (optimization: only recompute affected resources)\n          \u2514\u2500> Sets PushVersion = NextVersion() (timestamp-based)\n      \u2514\u2500> Stores in Environment.SetPushContext(push)\n      \u2514\u2500> Drops cache entries for affected resource types\n```\n\n**Step 4: Broadcast to All Proxies**\n```\nAdsPushAll(pushRequest)\n  \u2514\u2500> Iterates DiscoveryServer.adsClients\n      \u2514\u2500> For each Connection:\n          \u2514\u2500> Queues pushConnection() to pushQueue\n              \u2514\u2500> concurrentPushLimit semaphore regulates parallelism\n                  \u2514\u2500> computeProxyState(proxy, pushRequest)\n                      - Recomputes proxy's sidecar scope (if VirtualService affects it)\n                      - Scope determines which services/routes are relevant\n                  \u2514\u2500> Calls pushXds() for each watched resource type\n                      \u2514\u2500> findGenerator(typeURL, connection)\n                          - Selects appropriate generator (LdsGenerator, RdsGenerator, etc.)\n                      \u2514\u2500> gen.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, pushRequest)\n                          - Translates Istio config to Envoy proto\n                          - Uses PushContext snapshot from pushRequest\n                      \u2514\u2500> If gen.Generate() returns a DiscoveryResponse:\n                          \u2514\u2500> Sends over gRPC stream to proxy\n                              \u2514\u2500> Proxy ACKs with version/nonce\n```\n\n**Step 5: Proxy Receives Update**\n```\nEnvoy Proxy (receiving DiscoveryResponse for RDS)\n  \u2514\u2500> Parses RouteConfiguration from response\n      \u2514\u2500> Validates routes (checks all upstream clusters exist)\n      \u2514\u2500> Sends ACK with nonce from DiscoveryResponse\n          \u2514\u2500> DiscoveryServer records: proxy config updated successfully\n      \u2514\u2500> Hot-reloads routes without dropping active connections\n```\n\n**Performance Metrics:**\n- `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds`: How long to rebuild push context\n- `pilot_debounce_time`: Total delay from config change to push queue\n- `pilot_xds_push_time`: Per-proxy push generation time\n- `pilot_xds_calls_total`: Number of xDS Generate() calls\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nThe Discovery Service is designed with several extension points for custom behavior:\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\nUsers can inject custom `XdsResourceGenerator` implementations:\n\n```go\ntype CustomGenerator struct{}\n\nfunc (g *CustomGenerator) Generate(proxy *model.Proxy, w *model.WatchedResource, req *model.PushRequest) ([]*discovery.Resource, model.XdsLogDetails, error) {\n  // Custom logic to generate Envoy resources\n  // E.g., fetch data from external API, apply custom transformations\n  return resources, logDetails, nil\n}\n\n// Register in bootstrap\ngenerators[\"custom-type/lds\"] = &CustomGenerator{}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom load balancing logic (e.g., weighted round-robin based on external metrics)\n- Dynamic cluster configuration (e.g., auto-discovery of database hosts)\n- Security policy injection (e.g., enforce custom TLS settings)\n\n**Location:** Registered in `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/discovery.go`\n\n### 2. Service Registry Plugins\n\nCustom service discovery backends can be plugged in:\n\n```go\ntype CustomRegistry struct{}\n\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) Services() []*model.Service {\n  // Query external service registry (Consul, Eureka, etc.)\n}\n\n// Register as additional registry\naggregate.AddRegistry(customRegistry)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Integrate legacy service discovery (Consul, Eureka)\n- Cloud-provider-specific service discovery\n- Custom endpoint selection logic\n\n### 3. Authorization Policies\n\nDiscoveryServer supports pluggable authorization:\n\n```go\ntype CustomAuthorizer struct{}\n\nfunc (a *CustomAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attributes ...string) error {\n  // Custom authorization logic (e.g., check external RBAC system)\n  return nil // or error if unauthorized\n}\n\n// Configure in Pilot\nenv.Authorizers = append(env.Authorizers, &CustomAuthorizer{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- External RBAC systems (LDAP, OIDC)\n- Custom certificate validation\n- Traffic policy enforcement\n\n### 4. Event Handlers\n\nServices and configs support custom event handlers:\n\n```go\nhandler := func(event model.Event) {\n  // React to configuration changes\n  // E.g., update external systems, trigger deployments\n}\n\ncontroller.AppendServiceHandler(handler)\nconfigController.RegisterEventHandler(handler)\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Trigger canary deployments on config changes\n- Sync Pilot config to other systems\n- Custom audit logging\n\n### 5. Config Transformations via EnvoyFilter\n\nUsers can inject custom Envoy configuration without modifying Pilot:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3\nkind: EnvoyFilter\nmetadata:\n  name: custom-filter\nspec:\n  workloadSelector:\n    labels:\n      app: myapp\n  configPatches:\n  - applyTo: HTTP_FILTER\n    match:\n      context: SIDECAR_INBOUND\n    patch:\n      operation: INSERT_BEFORE\n      value:\n        name: envoy.filters.network.http_connection_manager\n        # ... custom filter config\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Configuration Validation Errors\n\nIf a VirtualService or DestinationRule has invalid syntax:\n\n1. ConfigController's validator rejects it before storing\n2. If already stored but later invalid:\n   - Generators detect missing referenced resources\n   - Log warnings/errors in proxy status\n   - Continue serving (fail-safe, don't drop proxies)\n\n**Visible in:**\n- Proxy push status: `ProxyStatus[error_code][proxy_id]`\n- Debug endpoints: `/debug/push_status`, `/debug/pushcontext`\n- Prometheus metrics: `pilot_proxy_status_*`\n\n### Push Failures\n\nIf a proxy disconnect during push:\n\n1. Connection closes (gRPC stream ends)\n2. `closeConnection()` removes from `adsClients`\n3. Remaining proxies continue receiving updates\n4. Proxy reconnects later, gets latest config\n\n### Service Registry Errors\n\nIf Kubernetes API is unavailable:\n\n1. Controller's sync loop stalls (but doesn't crash)\n2. `CachesSynced()` blocks, preventing Pilot readiness\n3. Once API recovers, resync occurs automatically\n4. Proxies remain connected, use cached configuration\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Push Scaling\n\nFor a mesh with N proxies:\n\n1. **Push Context Init**: O(1) per config change (not per proxy)\n2. **Per-Proxy Generation**: O(N) proxies \u00d7 O(M) config \u2192 O(N\u00d7M) total\n3. **Concurrency**: Limited by `concurrentPushLimit` (default: 100)\n   - Prevents overwhelming Pilot's CPU and memory\n   - Trade-off: slower update propagation in very large clusters\n\n### Debouncing\n\nRapid config changes are coalesced:\n\n- 10 VirtualService changes in 50ms \u2192 1 push context init (not 10)\n- Trade-off: 100ms delay vs. recomputation cost\n- Configurable via `DebounceAfter`, `DebounceMax`\n\n### Caching\n\nXDS resources are cached to avoid re-generation:\n\n- Keyed by proxy ID + resource type + config hash\n- Cleared on config change (invalidation is simple hash-based)\n- Significantly speeds up subsequent requests for same resource\n\n---\n\n## Source Files Reference\n\n| Component | File |\n|-----------|------|\n| DiscoveryServer (core) | `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` |\n| ADS stream handling | `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` |\n| Delta XDS | `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go` |\n| PushContext | `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` |\n| Config translation | `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` |\n| CDS (Cluster Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go` |\n| EDS (Endpoint Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` |\n| LDS (Listener Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go` |\n| RDS (Route Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go` |\n| SDS (Secret Discovery) | `pilot/pkg/xds/sds.go` |\n| Kubernetes service registry | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go` |\n| Aggregate registry | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go` |\n| ServiceEntry registry | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/controller.go` |\n| Bootstrap & initialization | `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/discovery.go`, `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/server.go` |\n| Testing utilities | `pilot/test/xds/fake.go` |\n| Metrics | `pilot/pkg/xds/monitoring.go` |\n| Debug handlers | `pilot/pkg/xds/debug.go` |\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Istio Pilot Discovery Service is a sophisticated distributed system that translates high-level mesh configuration into concrete Envoy proxy updates. Its architecture emphasizes:\n\n1. **Scalability**: Deferred initialization, debouncing, caching, and concurrency controls\n2. **Correctness**: Monotonically increasing versions, lock-free reads via snapshots\n3. **Extensibility**: Pluggable generators, registries, authorizers, and event handlers\n4. **Observability**: Comprehensive metrics, debug endpoints, and error tracking\n\nUnderstanding these layers is crucial for:\n- Debugging mesh configuration issues\n- Tuning Pilot performance for large clusters\n- Extending Istio with custom logic\n- Troubleshooting proxy synchronization problems\n",

# Istio Pilot's Discovery Service Architecture

## Overview

Istio's **Pilot Discovery Service** is the core control plane component that implements Envoy's xDS (Extensible Discovery Service) protocol, translating Istio's high-level networking configuration into concrete, proxy-ready Envoy resources. This document details the architecture of this subsystem, focusing on how configuration flows from Kubernetes API servers and Istio resources through Pilot to connected Envoy proxies.

At its core, the Discovery Service answers three fundamental questions for every connected Envoy proxy:
1. **What services exist** and where are their endpoints? (EDS/CDS)
2. **How should traffic route** to those services? (RDS/LDS)
3. **What security policies apply** to this traffic? (SDS/RBAC)

The Discovery Service does this by maintaining a push-based streaming connection with each proxy, broadcasting updates whenever the mesh configuration changes.

---

## 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server

**Location:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`

The `DiscoveryServer` is Pilot's central component implementing Envoy's xDS v3 protocol. It manages proxy connections, orchestrates configuration updates, and implements both state-of-the-world (SotW) and incremental (delta) xDS APIs.

### Core Structure

```go
type DiscoveryServer struct {
  Env *model.Environment              // Mesh configuration, service registry, config store
  Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator  // Type-specific config generators
  adsClients map[string]*Connection   // Active proxy connections
  pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest // Debouncing buffer
  pushQueue *PushQueue                // Queue for rate-limited pushes
  Cache model.XdsCache                // xDS resource cache
}
```

### Connection Lifecycle
